## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The governing equation is Newton's second law with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and possibly external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear + driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Coupled position-velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v**2 (polynomial expansion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces ŌåÆ only odd powers of x (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) appear, reflecting symmetric potential wells
- Energy-conserving systems ŌåÆ no velocity-dependent terms and no explicit time dependence in the acceleration equation
- Self-sustained oscillations ŌåÆ velocity terms with sign-changing coefficient like (1 - c*x┬▓)*v indicate limit cycle behavior (Van der Pol type)
- Hardening vs softening springs ŌåÆ sign of the cubic coefficient x┬│ relative to the linear term x determines frequency-amplitude relationship
- Periodic driving forces ŌåÆ explicit sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates forced oscillation
- Dissipative systems ŌåÆ odd-power velocity terms (v, v┬│) or v*|v| provide energy loss mechanisms
- Phase-space symmetry ŌåÆ if system is invariant under (xŌåÆ-x, vŌåÆ-v), only odd-order terms in x and v survive
- Pendulum-type nonlinearity ŌåÆ sin(c*x) replaces polynomial restoring force for large-angle oscillations
